  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_337bec99-8441-42fa-9895-82bae250d34c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer10159210983722003966">▶ <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37834800-siege-and-storm' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alternative Cover Edition #1</a>

  <span id="freeText10159210983722003966" style="display:none">▶ <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37834800-siege-and-storm" rel="nofollow noopener">Alternative Cover Edition #1</a>
</i><br /><br /><b>Darkness never dies.</b><br /><br />Hunted across the True Sea, haunted by the lives she took on the Fold, Alina must try to make a life with Mal in an unfamiliar land, all while keeping her identity as the Sun Summoner a secret. But she can’t outrun her past or her destiny for long.<br /><br />The Darkling has emerged from the Shadow Fold with a terrifying new power and a dangerous plan that will test the very boundaries of the natural world. With the help of a notorious privateer, Alina returns to the country she abandoned, determined to fight the forces gathering against Ravka. But as her power grows, Alina slips deeper into the Darkling’s game of forbidden magic, and farther away from Mal. Somehow, she will have to choose between her country, her power, and the love she always thought would guide her—or risk losing everything to the oncoming storm.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10159210983722003966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't think so, I was not really fond of the first one and the second one went downhill for me. After the first book I was actually giving up on the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't think so, I was not really fond of the first one and the second one went downhill for me. After the first book I was actually giving up on the trilogy, but I made the stupid decision of buying the three of them together, so I felt like it was a waste of money to give up this early and the least I could do was read. Not worth it. Now it looks like a waste of money and time!<br /><br />I was hoping her heart would be a little more decided in this one...Uh-uh not happening. The book itself was just a bunch of indecision and worthless happenings. About the action... Well, there was much more but in some specific moments. VERY SPECIFIC.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1126496163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1126496163" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1126496163?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1126496163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13542681198222577513"><b>Yup, I'm still insanely in love with the Darkling. I'm going to burn in Hell. Or rule the world with him as his Queen of Darkness, whatever comes first.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434207975ra/15183060.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I know the truth in your heart. The loneliness. The growing knowledge of your own difference. The ache of it.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>Alina tried to deny it, the connection and the similarities with him, but she could't hide from the truth. Her purpose seemed clear; rebuild the Second Army, defeat the Darkling, destroy the Fold, free Ravka, find the third a</span>
  <span id="freeText13542681198222577513" style="display:none"><b>Yup, I'm still insanely in love with the Darkling. I'm going to burn in Hell. Or rule the world with him as his Queen of Darkness, whatever comes first.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434207975ra/15183060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I know the truth in your heart. The loneliness. The growing knowledge of your own difference. The ache of it.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Alina tried to deny it, the connection and the similarities with him, but she could't hide from the truth. Her purpose seemed clear; rebuild the Second Army, defeat the Darkling, destroy the Fold, free Ravka, find the third amplifier, don't burn everyone in the process and keep Mal close. It wasn't simple though. She could feel the hunger for power growing inside her. With an ambitious prince by her side, she tried to fight the evil that was haunting Ravka and her guilt for helping this darkness unleash. Some people worshipped her as a Saint, some hated her because they were afraid of her powers and some wanted her to run away from this new life and become the person she was before she had the potential to destroy the world .Well, not some people, just Mal.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“There is no ordinary life for people like you and me.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>I really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061955.Siege_and_Storm__The_Grisha___2_" title="Siege and Storm (The Grisha, #2) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a> (not as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> but still it <i>was</i> great),a nd even my <u>dislike</u> of Mal can't take that away. You may ask why I don't like the handsome tracker who is willing to give his life for Alina, who bleeds when you cut her and tries to protect her at any cost. Because <b>he loves only certain parts of her</b>, excluding her being a Grisha and the role she has to play in the game of politics and eventually the struggle between light and darkness. He loves the girl who grew up with him, who followed him blindly and was always in the backround. <i>The girl he took for granted</i>. But she isn't the same person anymore, and the Darkling is the one to blame. The ruthless, murderous, manipulative Darkling. Deep, deep inside, I hope he will redeem himself, that <b>there is still something good worth saving</b> despite the awful things he has done, his twisted ways and his greed.<br><br>But Darkling isn't the only one antagonizing Mal. Have you met Nikolai?<br>The witty, sarcastic, calculative pirate (or <i>privateer</i>) with a claim to the throne who has a kind heart even though he rarely reveals it?<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"I can’t decide if you’re crazy or stupid."<br>"I have so many good qualities. It can be hard to choose."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392033010ra/8490181.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well after babbling about the men I want to marry (that's right, <i>men</i>, <u>I'm polygamic when it comes to book boyfriends</u>) I have to talk about the rest of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061955.Siege_and_Storm__The_Grisha___2_" title="Siege and Storm (The Grisha, #2) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a> !It was <b>captivating</b> (again, not as much as the first book but I can't give it less stars, it's physically impossible!), it sucked you in the world of the Grisha and held you with a strong grip. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a>'s <b>writing</b> is stunning, the <b>world-building </b>incredible, the <b>tension</b> in the scenes palpable and the evolution of Alina's character well-presented. Definitely <b>a great sequel to a great series</b>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13542681198222577513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2334626169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2334626169" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2334626169?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2334626169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17079520582239228542">how can this book have been so much better than book one, or book three, and yet still... not good?<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You just punched a prince, Alina. I guess we can add one more act of treason to our list.”<br/>I shook out my sore hand. My knuckles smarted. “First of all, are we so sure he really is a prince? And second, you’re just jealous.”<br/>“Of course I’m jealous. I thought I was going to get to punch him. That isn’t the point.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>2 1/2 stars, again. Again, very mixed feelings, so I’m going to start by tal</span>
  <span id="freeText17079520582239228542" style="display:none">how can this book have been so much better than book one, or book three, and yet still... not good?<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You just punched a prince, Alina. I guess we can add one more act of treason to our list.”<br />I shook out my sore hand. My knuckles smarted. “First of all, are we so sure he really is a prince? And second, you’re just jealous.”<br />“Of course I’m jealous. I thought I was going to get to punch him. That isn’t the point.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />2 1/2 stars, again. Again, very mixed feelings, so I’m going to start by talking about why this book is BETTER!<br /><br />First of all, way better plot! Bigger scope! Higher stakes! More interesting buildup! YOU DON’T KNOW WHAT’S GOING TO HAPPEN EVER! I know nothing really happens, but it manages to be so high tension anyway. Not to be all writer-y, but you can totally tell that Bardugo knows what she’s doing with dramatic tension now. She has that shit far more in control. And also there’s <b>
  <u>political intrigue</u>
</b> with Nikolai and Vasili! Except this is the non-boring kind of political intrigue. I support this political intrigue and not the bad excuse for political intrigue the first book offers. <br /><br />Second of all, char-ac-ter-de-vel-op-ment. I suddenly like Alina! I suddenly really like Alina, who is exploring her dark side. Wish the narrative would let this series get as dark as it deserves to be and will discuss that down below!!<br /><br />As a last note, I know everyone says this, but I love Nikolai. I think my mother might actually be <i>in</i> love with Nikolai. This might have something to do with him being the only non-shitty guy in this whole love triangular pyramid. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Mal crossed his arms and considered the privateer. "I can't decide if you're crazy or stupid."<br />"I have so many good qualities," Nikolai said. "It can be hard to choose.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The thing is, this book is a huge improvement over book one, but it’s still not really all that good? <br /><br />I will admit, on a small note, I thought the beginning of this book was kind of shitty. A thing happens in the first, like, four pages that negates everything that happened in the prologue or at the very end of the last book. Entire plot points could have been skipped. Why.<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>→ the love pyramid ←</b>
</i><br />All of you failed basic geometry, because this is not a love square, it is a love triangular pyramid. In which one of the ends is rotted, one is also maybe banging a different point of a different triangular pyramid, and one has zero chemistry with the point of the triangular pyramid but is so awesome that he’s the best option by default. <br /><br />Yeah, I don't like this triangle very much. Shocker. Mostly because the Darkling is a burnt chicken nugget and I hate him, and I might actually find his villain-y character really intriguing, but the fact that he is discussed as a viable love interest on this website is creepy. <br /><br />But the issue isn't even really with the love triangle! It's with the fact that the love triangle is there to build into love drama that takes away from the seriousness of the plot. So let's discuss the real trouble here:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>→ all the petty drama ←</b>
</i><br /><b>
  <u>We Need To Talk About Mal.</u>
</b> Who is suddenly an asshole and I understand why everyone likes Nikolai better. But... okay. I actually think his motivations make a lot of sense? Yeah, he's being a dick, but he's not being an abuser (as much of the discourse on book twitter has previously seemed to imply). More than anything, I'm simply bored by him.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"'Not my type, but handsome.'<br />My brows shot up. In my experience, Mal was just about everyone's type."</i>
</blockquote><br />There’s this moment where Tamar says Mal “isn’t her type” and Alina is literally like “but Mal is EVERYONE’S type” and although A) I call bullshit on that, I also think it's absolutely hilarious that B) the line is meant to indicate Tamar is a lesbian. [Okay, yeah, I actually knew that going in.] <br /><br /><i>
  <b>→ the real problem ←</b>
</i><br />But the problem isn't even <i>really</i> with Mal. Or <i>really</i> with Alina. The problem is <b>
  <u>the narrative of this book just <i>will not</i> let this series get as dark as it deserves to be.</u>
</b> This series is one about awful characters doing awful things in which the lead is basically slowly losing her humanity and the villain is maybe possibly doing it for the right reasons and the love interest is insecure and the princes are shitty and really, <b>no one is doing the right thing, and certainly not for the right reasons.</b> <b>
  <u>But it refuses to let itself be this.</u>
</b> I keep feeling Bardugo come <i>thiiis</i> close to inner darkness and antihero power and then shying away. <br /><br />I respect that the YA market a few years ago was very different, that we ate up that Zoya-makes-Alina-jealous plotline and weren't so invested in Alina's glorious antiherodom. But I really think this series is wasted potential personified.<br /><br />Yeah. Those are my thoughts. I am not a fan. I'm really disappointed in how much I am not a fan.<br /><br /><a href="https://ellexamines.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/ellexamines/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4F6I" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="https://ellexamines.carrd.co/" rel="nofollow noopener">About</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17079520582239228542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_573435119" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/573435119" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/573435119?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer573435119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3369907560000610140"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>This rating might come as a surprise after I was so excited to get reacquainted with the Darkling in my early status update. However, if it hadn't been for the scenes with the Darkling, this book would have probably only received one star - it's only his characterisation, his different layers and, let's face it, his sexiness that convinced me to rate this at two stars. Maybe I could stretch to 2.5 if I close my eyes and picture the Darkling like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415203i/819534.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I usually approach the sequels to three s</span>
  <span id="freeText3369907560000610140" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This rating might come as a surprise after I was so excited to get reacquainted with the Darkling in my early status update. However, if it hadn't been for the scenes with the Darkling, this book would have probably only received one star - it's only his characterisation, his different layers and, let's face it, his sexiness that convinced me to rate this at two stars. Maybe I could stretch to 2.5 if I close my eyes and picture the Darkling like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415203i/819534.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I usually approach the sequels to three star reads with some trepidation but I confess that my hopes were high for this one. Despite the flaws present throughout <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a>, I found it wildly entertaining in parts and a very easy page-turner. I had also hoped that Alina would mature and grow once she harnessed her power and realised that some things are more important than beauty and looks - this realisation never came. In fact, I believe the relationship between beauty and power to be even more apparent in this sequel and I struggle to sympathise with a girl who discovers she is incredibly powerful but still can't see her worth beyond her plain appearance.<br><br>This I just mentioned is nothing new and was a problem for me in the first installment which has unfortunately carried over into the second. However, the main difference between the two that overrides everything else and is way bigger than my problems with the beauty issue - which I may have otherwise been able to look past - is that I found this second book incredibly boring. Or I did at least after the first quarter where the Darkling disappears for a huge chunk of the book (honestly, he is the only interesting thing about this series). Gone was the fun I had while reading book one, gone was the exciting mystery and sexual tension. This book introduced several new characters who I never came to care about, whilst also bringing Alina Shallowkova and whiny Mal back into the spotlight.<br><br>Mal is a dull character. He is whiny, uninteresting and I can see no reason why anyone would think the sun shines out of his backside... yes, even Alina. Though, saying that, he is radiantly gorgeous and I suppose Alina doesn't need any more of a reason to put someone on a pedestal. I was so bored by their relationship that I couldn't even summon the energy for my standard eyeroll reserved for fictional couples that are annoying. I'm not even sure what Mal does for most of this book aside from standing by and being jealous of every man that Alina talks to.<br><br>I admit that I was far less engaged for the second half of the book, so if someone would like to come and tell me that something awesome happened while I was away floating on a cloud of not caring, that really wouldn't surprise me. Most of it was read without interest, some bits were even skimmed. I think it's fair to say that I won't be returning for the next book. Such a shame because I was genuinely very excited for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061955.Siege_and_Storm__The_Grisha___2_" title="Siege and Storm (The Grisha, #2) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Siege and Storm</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3369907560000610140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1015907457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015907457" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1015907457?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1015907457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11210186885844362605">5 stars!<br/><br/>I really loved <i>Siege & Storm</i>! I had not delved into the Grishaverse Trilogy since reading book one in 2015, and I am saddened that it took me so long to go back to this amazing world!<br/><br/>I definitely struggled with the beginning of this book, but I feel it is a reflection of myself instead of the quality of the book. I’ve realized that jumping into sequels of books I haven’t read in years via audiobook is a habit I should break as I don’t retain much from the beginning on the story, but none</span>
  <span id="freeText11210186885844362605" style="display:none">5 stars!<br /><br />I really loved <i>Siege &amp; Storm</i>! I had not delved into the Grishaverse Trilogy since reading book one in 2015, and I am saddened that it took me so long to go back to this amazing world!<br /><br />I definitely struggled with the beginning of this book, but I feel it is a reflection of myself instead of the quality of the book. I’ve realized that jumping into sequels of books I haven’t read in years via audiobook is a habit I should break as I don’t retain much from the beginning on the story, but nonetheless once I finally got engaged, I was HOOKED.<br /><br />I love these characters and the way they develop in the second installment. I love this world. I love the magic system. I love the plot. I love everything about this book and I am immediately going to dive into book three to avoid what happened at the beginning of this novel. XD<br /><br />I apologize that this isn’t the most in-depth review – The Grisha Trilogy is one where I just can’t do anything but gush about it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11210186885844362605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3042111623" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3042111623" />
    <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess"><img alt="The Burning Rose (Jess)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605317941p2/48477217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3042111623?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Burning Rose (Jess)" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess">The Burning Rose (Jess)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3042111623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3536466239901958151">5/5 stars.<br/>This book was a thousand times better than the first.<br/>The characters have improved, the plot has improved. It was thrilling, interesting, intriguing, it gave me the feeling that I couldn't put the book out of my hands. Anything that Lehigh Bardugo put into the plot in this book certainly helped the story. It's as if she saved herself with this plot.<br/><br/>The first addition I would like to point out is the pirates. I'm not sure what about you, but in my opinion, when pirates are involved, it's</span>
  <span id="freeText3536466239901958151" style="display:none">5/5 stars.<br />This book was a thousand times better than the first.<br />The characters have improved, the plot has improved. It was thrilling, interesting, intriguing, it gave me the feeling that I couldn't put the book out of my hands. Anything that Lehigh Bardugo put into the plot in this book certainly helped the story. It's as if she saved herself with this plot.<br /><br />The first addition I would like to point out is the pirates. I'm not sure what about you, but in my opinion, when pirates are involved, it's much more interesting. Although this is a bit of a risky matter, because a plot with pirates is very critical- either it's super excellent or it's bad. In this matter, the pirates saved Bardugo. Mostly Sturmhond, which I will mention later.<br /> <br />Let's talk about the darkling.<br />This fellow is invincible, how lovely, I'm all for it.<br />If you know me, you know how much I admire this character. Frankly, I think he’s the most intriguing character in this series. If it weren't for the darkling, these books wouldn't have been interesting.<br /><br />In my review of the first book, I mentioned that Alina is a good character but not interesting enough. In this book her character is fantastic. Everything Alina has experienced made her to be a good character. And the biggest credit goes to the Darkling. Yes, him again. Applaud him, people, he deserves it. There’s nothing like a villain who deserves to be a villain.<br /><br />Now, as I promised, there’s another character that I think has made this plot fascinating, and his nickname is Sturmhond, whose real name we discover in the middle of the book. This is a special, volatile character, totally intriguing. I found myself wishing to read more about him, to know him better. It’s so easy to love him, and it’s remarkable and commendable.<br /><br />I'm not sure if I want to put Mal into this review, just as I wish he wasn't in the book. I know it sounds cruel, but I don't like him. And most importantly, I don't like his influence on Alina, unlike the other characters, who surround Alina and affect her (whether it's for the worse or for the better), it feels to me that Mal just lowers her even further to the bottom. On the other hand, I do know that if it wasn't for him, the plot would have been completely different, I don't know if for the better or not, and he did help Alina and was there for her. Maybe I just hope his character and influence were a little different. <br />In the first book he was like a distant figure, found mainly in Alina's thoughts. But he's an important character in this book, and I really wished he wasn't. Half of the book Alina worried and thought about Mal, which is tiring.<br /><br />In addition, I would like to commend Leigh Bardugo for her writing. She writes excellently, her style is incredible and that makes her books more interesting. There’s a feeling in the background of a fog that makes everything invisible except what is on your hands.<br />I really liked the attention she gave Alina in this book. Like I said, Alina's character has improved. In this book, Alina realized that she and the darkling are equally unique and probably also just as powerful. Alina finally believes in her ability and ready to fight the Darkling , she even stole his spot, lol. I was so proud of her.<br />And I was proud of the darkling too. He survives, brave, charismatic, and oh my, how much I die for his sensitivity to Alina. I don't usually do that, but this time I definitely wish they were together. They are so matched, and he’s so right that no one can understand her the way he understands her.<br /><br />I know there are other characters in the book that are worth talking about, but I decided not to overdo my reviews because they are always overly long, so I'll end the review here, thank you for reading.<br /><br />P.S. Oh my God! My sweet Jenna?!?!?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3536466239901958151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2500514396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2500514396" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2500514396?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/18525661-siege-and-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2500514396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7298556202933666896"><i>”You know the problem with heroes and saints, Nikolai?” I asked as I closed the book’s cover and headed for the door. “They always end up dead.”</i><br/><br/>Do you know the song <b>“One to Make Her Happy”</b> from Marque? No? That’s unfortunate, because while I read this book I had a horrible earworm and couldn’t get it out of my head. I was basically humming it the entire time and decided to change the name from Daisy to Alina. I’m sure by now you’re curious about the lyrics and I’m happy to oblige:<br/><br/><i>“One to make he</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7298556202933666896" style="display:none"><i>”You know the problem with heroes and saints, Nikolai?” I asked as I closed the book’s cover and headed for the door. “They always end up dead.”</i><br /><br />Do you know the song <b>“One to Make Her Happy”</b> from Marque? No? That’s unfortunate, because while I read this book I had a horrible earworm and couldn’t get it out of my head. I was basically humming it the entire time and decided to change the name from Daisy to Alina. I’m sure by now you’re curious about the lyrics and I’m happy to oblige:<br /><br /><i>“One to make her happy (Mal)<br />One to make her sad (The Darkling)<br />One to give her good love<br />That she never had (Nikolai)<br /><s>Daisy</s> Alina and her boyfriends <br />Livin’ in a house<br />Sharing just a good life. <br />That was four years ago.<br />Now <s>Daisy</s> Alina blew the whole show.”</i><br /><br />Very suitable, right? *lol* I swear to read <b>“Siege and Storm”</b> really felt like Alina and I had 3 different boyfriends because seriously, who’s able to choose between all those awesome boys? I just love them all for different reasons and if forced to make a decision I’m afraid I couldn’t even choose for the life of me. XD They are all great and they all have their pros and cons. ;-P Still, it would be a lie if I’d claim that Nikolai didn’t make me swoon. Such an awesome man! *sighs deeply* Then again The Darkling is still hot and Mal is still sweet so … <b>URGH!!!</b> See what I’m talking about? *lol*<br /><br />Guess Alina and I will have to be Daisy for a little while longer. ;-) Hopefully book three will make it easier to choose. XD Still, the ending of <b>“Siege and Storm”</b> was heavy and I really don’t know what Leigh is going to come up with in the last book. I bet she has a lot in store for us and truth be told, I’m not entirely sure if I’m ready. Haha! <br /><br />Seems like I’ll just have to dive into it and find out though! ;-)<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><u>
  <b>I’m afraid there will be lots of spoilers in here because the fate of some of the characters really made me go all: WOW!! NO!! ARGH!! WHY?! So consider yourself warned! This is the cupboard door to my spoiler section and if you don’t want to be spoiled you better don’t enter my personal Narnia. ;-P</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Alina:</b><br /><br /><i>”I don’t care if you think I’m a Saint or a fool or the Darklings’s whore. If you want to remain at the Little Palace, you will follow me. And if you don’t like it, you will be gone by tonight, or I will have you in chains. I am a soldier. I am the Sun Summoner. And I’m the only chance you have.”</i> <br /><br />I think I liked Alina more in this one! She was no longer the naïve heroine and finally started to show her claws. *lol* Hard to say if this was due to the influence of Nikolai or because of what happened with the Darkling, no matter the reason I’m still glad she decided to take the reins and did what needed to be done. Some might argue that she’s too young for all this but considering how long the Darkling was able to fool everyone around him I think it’s safe to say that Alina really might be their best bet. XD The ending however was quite heavy! I mean poor girl! If she’s already so weak and broken how is the Darkling going to fare? I really don’t know in which direction book 3 will go and because this rarely happens I’m more than just intrigued. ;-) I hope Alina won’t die, I really do.<br /><br /><b>The Darkling:</b><br /><br /><i>The faint tracery of scars on his face was barely visible, like the ghost of a map. One ran perilously close to his right eye. He’d almost lost it. He cupped my cheek with his hand, and when he spoke, his voice was almost tender. “They’re just the beginning,” he whispered.</i><br /><br /><b>WOAH!!</b> Well, the Darkling was quite a surprise in this one. I always knew that he’s ruthless and prone to cruelty; I didn’t expect him to go all DARK though. *lol* I think it might have to do with what happened at the Fold and I’m pretty sure that he lost the grip on his own darkness. It’s just a theory but in the first book it was <u>him</u> who controlled the darkness and guided it to do his bidding and I think that this changed drastically. Now it seems more like the darkness got a hold of him and is consuming him in order to achieve its goals. Would explain why he’s so drained by the nichevo’ya he creates. Still, I can’t really hate him for what he’s done because he’s just a too good villain and I always appreciate a good villain when I see one. *lol* Hmm… maybe he can still be saved? <br /><br /><b>Mal:</b><br /><br /><i>”Easy, now. Mustn’t get blood on the uniform. Let me explain – “<br />“Try explaining with my first in your mouth.”</i> <br /><br />Haha! Mal! I can’t help but like that boy! His honesty is so refreshing and the fact he never bothers to filter his thoughts is very entertaining. *lol* Even after finishing the second book I still don’t get why so many people seem to hate him. He’s a nice and decent guy and I think everything he said and did was justified. Yes, he didn’t have to drink himself senseless and gamble in the bars but it was his only way to deal with his situation and you can’t really blame him for it. At least I don’t. Life is tough, we all have our vices and try our best to deal with the cards that we’re given. It’s obvious that he loves Alina more than anything and it’s also rather plain that this love started to destroy and poison him. Plus Alina really wasn’t the most understanding person. So yes, I still like Mal and I’m not sorry about it!!! &lt;3 <br /><br /><i>”And there’s no way I’m leaving you alone with Prince Perfect.”<br />“So you don’t trust me to resist his charms?”<br />“I don’t even trust myself.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Nikolai:</b><br /><br /><i>I blew out a frustrated breath. “Do you ever answer a question directly?”<br />“Hard to say. Ah, there, I’ve done it again.”</i><br /><br /><b>OH BOY!!!</b> Nikolai is so awesome!! I can’t even!! &lt;333 Yes, I’m having a crazy fangirl moment here but seriously, what’s not to love?! This guy is amazing and I just love everything about him. His attitude, his cunning plans, his many different faces, his compassion and passion. Well, basically everything that comes out of his mouth. *lol* Leigh truly outdid herself when she created this wonderful man and I’ll be forever thankful that she wrote him down on paper! &lt;3 I love that he has principles and rules he lives by and if things would have gone my way Vasily wouldn’t even have gotten close to the throne. It’s obvious that Nikolai is the best choice and I really hope that there’ll be something left of Ravka once he’s able to rule! Still, right now I don’t know what happened to him and this is such a mean move! *lol* Leigh what happened to Nikolai?!!! Guess I’ll have to read the last book soon! XD<br /><br /><i>”Now that’s a word best not used around me. I tend to be overfond of risk.”</i> <br /><br /><i>”You never improvise,” I said. “Everything you do is calculated. You change personalities the way other people change hats. And you know what? It’s creepy. Aren’t you ever just yourself?”<br />“I’m a prince, Alina. I can’t afford to be myself.”</i><br /><br /><i>”When people say impossible, they usually mean improbable.”</i><br /><br /><b>Genya:</b><br /><br /><i>”She and David stay behind the group. She can’t move very quickly.” He paused. “The pilgrims call her “Razrusha’ya.” <br />The Ruined.”</i> <br /><br />My poor, poor girl! T_T I can’t believe that the Darkling did this to her!!! She didn’t deserve this! Just because she helped Alina to flee? It’s not fair and I would have expected better from the Darkling! I mean I know he’s the villain but Genya was so loyal to him and that’s how he thanks her? My poor Genya! I just want to hug her and tell her that everything will get better and that she’s still the most beautiful woman of Ravka! &lt;333 I really hope David will do all those things because if not I’m going to kick him in his skinny behind. *lol*<br /><br /><b>The ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Alina &amp; The Darkling:</u><br /><br /><i>”He can’t wait to get away from you,” I said, hovering by the door. “He’s afraid of what you’ve become. They all are.”<br />“Do you fear me, Alina?”<br />“That’s what you want, isn’t it?”<br />The Darkling shrugged. “Fear is a powerful ally,” he said. “And loyal.”</i><br /><br />The moments between those two were rather short in this book and I really would have loved to see more of them together. They had such a nice chemistry in “Shadow and Bone” and despite everything Alina still seems to be drawn to him. Well, the Darkling certainly has an irresistible allure. Can’t blame her for it. ;-P Still, I hope I’ll get more of them in the last book because they are just too intriguing together. XD<br /><br /><u>Alina &amp; Mal:</u><br /><br /><i>”You wanted to wear the second amplifier. You have it. You want to go to Os Alta? Fine, we’ll go. You say you need the firebird. I’ll find a way to get it for you. But when all this is over, Alina, I wonder if you’ll still want me.”</i><br /><br />Aww those two killed me! It’s like they just can’t be together because the entire world and their own fate is against them. Alina can’t hand over her responsibility because she’s the only sun summoner and basically the only person who’s able to stop the Darkling and Mal can’t be at her side because he’d be like Icarus getting too close to the sun. T_T He doesn’t understand her powers and the need to use them and even though he doesn’t get it he still decided to be with her. Right now I really see no way how their relationship could be able to work out. I mean it’s not like Alina will stop being Grisha and Mal can’t stop being a tracker as well. *sighs* It’s such a muddled situation….<br /><br /><i>”Why didn’t you say something?”<br />“What could I say? And when? I barely see you anymore.”<br />“I thought you wanted to go.”<br />“I wanted you to ask me to stay.”</i> <br /><br /><u>Alina &amp; Nikolai:</u><br /><br /><i>”What’s a pirate doing on a whaler?” I asked.<br />“Privateer,” he corrected. “I have several ships. The Darkling wanted a whaler, so I got him one.”<br />“You mean you stole it.”<br />“Acquired it.”<br />“You were in my cabin.”<br />“Many women dream of me,” he said lightly as he steered me down the deck.</i><br /><br />Now those two!! *LOL* I lived for their conversations!! I swear Nikolai is so, so damn awesome! Did I already tell you how much I love this man?! I’m sure I did! Haha! Well, the chemistry between Alina and Nikolai was amazing as well and I can’t say how much I loved it that she wasn’t swooning and drooling all over him like everyone else! XD She saw him as a normal person and that’s what made their scenes so perfect. =) I think my favourite moment was the encounter at the lake and the fact that Nikolai turned her down, because he knew she’d only use him as a make-do. I love this man, I really, really do! &lt;333 For some reason I doubt that Alina will end up with him though. <br /><br /><i>”The Darkling will hunt you for the rest of your days.”<br />“Then you and I will have something in common, won’t we? Besides, I like to have powerful enemies. Makes me feel important.”<br />Mal crossed his arms and considered the privateer. “I can’t decide if you’re crazy or stupid.”<br />“I have so many good qualities,” Sturmhond said. “It can be hard to choose.”</i><br /><br /><i>”And what are you doing to be useful, your highness?”<br />“I’m a prince,” said Nikolai. “Being useful isn’t part of my job description. But,” he added, “when I’m not lazing about being handsome, I’ll be trying to better equip the First Army and gather intelligence on the Darkling’s location.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I want to kiss you,” Nikolai said. “But I won’t. Not until you’re thinking of me instead of trying to forget him.”</i><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />Once again I was hooked until the very end and once again I couldn’t help it and already started with the next book even though I didn’t even write my review for this one. I guess it’s safe to say that this series is really enjoyable and entertaining, especially now that Nikolai entered the scene!! ;-P<br />I can’t wait to read more about him and I want to see so much more of all of <s>Daisy’s</s> Alina’s other <s>boyfriends</s> love interests as well. *lol* <br /><br />So all I can say is: Happy Reading! I hope you’ll love “Siege and Storm” as much as I did! ;-)</span>

<div id="review_2746767267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2746767267" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2746767267?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780805094602" href="/book/show/37834800-siege-and-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2746767267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11644927444784441152"><b>4.2</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote>“When people say impossible, they usually mean improbable.” </blockquote><br/><br/><b>OH YES BABY. THAT'S THE SHIT I LIKE TO SEE.</b>And this how a very thorough and serious review begins, everybody! Take a seat and enjoy after this mini break for the plot summary!<br/><br/><i>Hunted across the True Sea, haunted by the lives she took on the Fold, Alina must try to make a life with Mal in an unfamiliar land. She finds starting new is not easy while keeping her identity as the Sun Summoner a secret. She can’t outrun her</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11644927444784441152" style="display:none"><b>4.2</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote>“When people say impossible, they usually mean improbable.” </blockquote><br /><br /><b>OH YES BABY. THAT'S THE SHIT I LIKE TO SEE.</b>And this how a very thorough and serious review begins, everybody! Take a seat and enjoy after this mini break for the plot summary!<br /><br /><i>Hunted across the True Sea, haunted by the lives she took on the Fold, Alina must try to make a life with Mal in an unfamiliar land. She finds starting new is not easy while keeping her identity as the Sun Summoner a secret. She can’t outrun her past or her destiny for long.<br /><br />The Darkling has emerged from the Shadow Fold with a terrifying new power and a dangerous plan that will test the very boundaries of the natural world. With the help of a notorious privateer, Alina returns to the country she abandoned, determined to fight the forces gathering against Ravka. But as her power grows, Alina slips deeper into the Darkling’s game of forbidden magic, and farther away from Mal. Somehow, she will have to choose between her country, her power, and the love she always thought would guide her--or risk losing everything to the oncoming storm.</i><br /><br />This book has left me in want for the next one. <b>WHAT AN ENDING MAN.</b> This book was exhilarating, intriguing, action packed, character driven, addicting e.t.c. It held so much more depth than its predecessor, it was basically the better version of the first book. The world was more fascinating, the politics more immersive and the characters more developed.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Alina</u>
</b><br />Her character certainly grew in this book. <b>From this weak frail insecure girl who envied everyone around her, couldn't fit in and didn't know how to manipulate her power she became a strong woman who could lead and harness her power to protect her country.</b> Her inner battle with the darkness she was feeling creeping in was very interesting to read about and it made her character much more than this one dimentional girl she was in book one. Don't get me wrong, she was still unlikable to me and not compelling enough to be the lead of the book, but she gained much more appreciation in my eyes after this book. I'm looking forward to see what more her character has to give.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Mal</u>
</b><br />Ugh! Where to begin. <b>I DON'T FUCKING LIKE HIM AT ALL.</b> I can't stand his fucking personality. This dude bothers me so much, I can't even fathom it. What does Alina see in him? <b>He's so boring, predictable, demanding, insecure and selfish</b>. He was unbearable in this book. I didn't mind his character at all in the first book, I just didn't have any interest in him. It's like he didn't exist. But in this book, he annoyed me to death. I (regrettably) know Alina is gonna end up with him, and I'm so disappointed. She should have ended up with the next <b>KICK ASS</b> character I'm gonna talk about.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>FUCKING NIKOLAI LANTSOV</u>
</b><br />Here I am introducing you, <b>MY CURRENT BOYFRIEND. I love him, I love him so much I want to cry. THANK YOU <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a> FOR THIS GEM OF A CHARACTER.</b> Look, this series doesn't really rely on characters. it relies on the beautiful world, the politics and the magic. But it's ok, you know, not every book is about characters. But this character came in and changed the game. <b>HE'S SO 3D.</b> He's funny, witty, interesting, compassionate, determined, a true fighter who do anything for his country and who never backs down even though he's been through lots of shit. I feel this series finally introduced us to a full on three dimentional character and I'm so happy. I wasn't expecting the twist that Sturmhond was Nikolai, I was pleasantly surprised. I knew the existence of this character long before, mostly because of Six of Crows and the new duology that is about him (I've already purchased the book, even though I haven't even finished the Grisha Trilogy <b>BUT WHO GIVES A FUCK</b>) but I thought we wouldn't see him in this trilogy. How happy I am to have been wrong. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The romance</u>
</b><br /><b>Nah.</b> The romance in this book is the least thing I cared about. It was much more impactful in the first book, but in this one it was totally stale. Something was about to happen when Nikolai came in the picture... but we all know he ain't got no chance. WHY ALINA. WHY. At this point, I don't really care who she ends up with, her with Mal don't tickle my pickle, her and the Darkling is hot but wrong, and her and Nikolai just won't happen. After all, this book isn't centered around characters and their relationships and shit. So, idgaf!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The plot</u>
</b><br />I truly enjoyed the fact that this book was much more fast paced than the previous one... it had more content to provide its readers. The first 100 and the last 100 pages were it for me, whereas the middle chunk of the book was more about planning and scheming the end battle. The first part of the book, which was at sea was certainly my fav... everything that happens at sea is my thing. I loved the magic system again, I loved the gorgeous and fulfilling world and I loved the angsty politics. I hope the next one will provide me the same gratification and even more<br /><br />All in all, I enjoyed this book much more than the first one, and I'm going into the third and final book fully prepared. <b>It was a fast paced and fantastic read which introduced me to my next bae, and kept hooked to it every single minute.</b> I'm anxious for the ending to be honest, and I'm also anxious for the next series. Well then, till the final book in this series, K BYE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11644927444784441152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17799948358122911234">I didn't enjoy this quite as much as the first book, and I think it's partly because of my dislike for Mal, and partly because I found the moments between the high action points to be too slow/dull for my taste. <br/><br/>My favourite thing about this book was some of the new characters we meet, especially Sturmhond! I was also a little sad we didn't see quite as much of the Darkling, he is such an interesting character.</span>

<div id="review_334406253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334406253" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334406253?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Duh. Everyone. #hairflip</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=macmillan">macmillan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-need-to-buy-this-book">i-need-to-buy-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=oh-yeah-baby">oh-yeah-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=yeah-baby-5-stars">yeah-baby-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-favorite">2013-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334406253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17964194335089437221">I always go into a second book in a series with fears that it will have the dreaded "Second Book Syndrome". I worry that the characters will regress, the plot will stall and surmount to overall ridiculousness, and in the end, become boring and lathered in disappointment. So even though <em>The Grisha</em> series is a new favorite for me, I still had these concerns. You cannot even imagine my glee when I discovered <em>Siege and Storm</em> did NOT suffer from any of these things. On the contrary, it was even <em>bette</em></span>
  <span id="freeText17964194335089437221" style="display:none">I always go into a second book in a series with fears that it will have the dreaded "Second Book Syndrome". I worry that the characters will regress, the plot will stall and surmount to overall ridiculousness, and in the end, become boring and lathered in disappointment. So even though <em>The Grisha</em> series is a new favorite for me, I still had these concerns. You cannot even imagine my glee when I discovered <em>Siege and Storm</em> did NOT suffer from any of these things. On the contrary, it was even <em>better</em> than its predecessor. If you loved <em>Shadow and Bone</em>, be prepared to be blown away!<br><br>There are so many things I want mention and squeal about in this review, but OH THE SPOILERS. And anyway, Kat did such a great job with <a title="Review: Siege and Storm by Leigh Bardugo" href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2013/03/02/review-siege-and-storm-by-leigh-bardugo/" rel="nofollow noopener">reviewing in code</a> already. So I've decided to just write letters.<br><br> <br><br>Dear Darkling,<br><br>You're so evil, but I can't seem to conjure up any feelings of dislike for you. In fact, I missed you in <em>Siege and Storm</em>. For most of the novel, you were gone from me, only appearing in Alina's dreams. How fair is that? Don't you know how much I need your evil goodness to be present at all times? Seeing you torture the poor peasants of the Grisha world, warms my heart.<br><br>And, oh, Darkling, what new skills you have. Wait, does that sound dirty? Because it totally isn't. Then again, you did tell us all to, "Make me your villain." It's only fair if I, too, am allowed at least one inappropriate pun. But seriously, you've leveled up faster than a Super Saiyan in <em>Siege and Storm</em>. Kat says you learned to line dance, but I think it's more along the line of baking cookies. You showed those cookies who was boss!<br><br>But your ending concerns me. I guess the cookie batter turned out to be much more difficult that you expected. Maybe you should take a page from Paula Deen and add more evil butter. I'm not sure this has anything to do with book 3, <em>Ruin and Rising</em>, but I just like cookies, okay? And you. I like you too. So be sure to be extra evil next time and give those cookies a run for their money.<br><br>Love,<br><br>Steph<br><br>--------------------<br><br>Dearest Mal,<br><br>Please do us all a favor and stop being so insecure over your relationship with Alina. The girl's got a lot on her plate. She has the responsibility of saving all of Ravka, which is kinda a tad more important than you. I need for you to be more understanding and supportive. I liked you in <em>Shadow and Bone</em>, but I'm starting to think I'm outgrowing my mildly inappropriate swooning of you. Just yesterday, I found myself wondering if Leigh might actually kill you off in <em>Ruin and Rising</em>. If that happens, it's possible I might only mourn you for half a page. No, no, no! I take it back! Don't you dare die on me, Mal-Mal!<br><br>True love is tough love,<br><br>Steph<br><br>P.S. I still love you, Mal. &lt;3<br><br>--------------------<br><br>Sturmhond,<br><br>I think I speak for everyone when I say, please become a real person.<br><br>xoxo,<br><br>Steph<br><br>========<br><br>And finally:<br><br>Dear Leigh,<br><br>Amazing.<br><br>You are evil. Evil, evil, evil. So evil, your stories leave me speechless. Your humor sends me into fits of giggles and tickles my tender pieces. Your plots make me wish I can pack my bags and vacate to your mind if only for a day. Please don't ever stop being this <del>awesome</del> evil. And because Troy gifs have become our thing:<br><p>
  <img alt=" photo troy_zpse5607e29.gif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380378508ra/734179.gif" width="500" height="275" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>Also, that ending is causing me to hit the <em>Kvas</em> pretty hard tonight. Look what you've done to me.<br><p>
  <img alt=" photo kvas_zpsa3b783e0.gif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380378508ra/734180.gif" width="500" height="281" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><p>
  <em>Mal, Darkling, Sturmhond... I must collect them all. </em>
</p><br><em>Hiccup</em>,<br><br>Steph<br><br> <br><br><em>An ARC was received for a review from the publisher. No monies or favors were exchanged for a positive review. Thanks, Macmillan! </em><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250044433" href="/book/show/35529904-siege-and-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2243274624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13790602100405412267">this reread has made me realise one important thing - we, the readers, were robbed in <i>‘king of scars.’</i> <br/><br/>nickolai lantsov, prince of ravka and my heart, grand duke of udova, sturmhond of the true sea and first of his name did not sacrifice so much for miss priss zoya to steal as much page time as she did. i cant stand her. sometimes i just wish she would summon water to drown herself. lol.<br/><br/>my anger aside, this series is, and still remains to be, the best ever. <br/><br/><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2002783577?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25532300-siege-and-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2002783577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17119548069096970321">Enjoyed the audio of this much more than my first time reading the print version!<br/><br/>******************<br/>Now listen here, I'm still on board with the series but about 70% of this book was SLLLLLOOOOOOWWWWW<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://WWW'>WWW</a>........<br/><br/><i>*super minor spoilers</i><br/><br/>While this was definitely an informative middle chapter to the trilogy, I can't help but be slightly disappointed that there just wasn't <b>more</b>. I found myself really excited in the final chapters with the sudden blaze of action, but couldn't help feeling like Bardugo sa</span>
  <span id="freeText17119548069096970321" style="display:none">Enjoyed the audio of this much more than my first time reading the print version!<br /><br />******************<br />Now listen here, I'm still on board with the series but about 70% of this book was SLLLLLOOOOOOWWWWW<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://WWW">WWW</a>........<br /><br /><i>*super minor spoilers</i><br /><br />While this was definitely an informative middle chapter to the trilogy, I can't help but be slightly disappointed that there just wasn't <b>more</b>. I found myself really excited in the final chapters with the sudden blaze of action, but couldn't help feeling like Bardugo saved all the fun stuff for the end in an attempt to make sure no one gave up on the series mid way. I needed more Darkling, I needed more Nikolai, I needed more action, but the only thing I got more of was Mal and Alina being awkward. I know it sounds like I'm pooping all over this book, and I really did enjoy it overall, it just went in a totally different direction than expected. I was really hoping to get more time with Nikolai in an attempt to broaden my shipping options but it seems I can't even do that. :( However, if you are a fan of Mal then you will really enjoy this one. <br /><br />There were some nice little twists that kept me from putting this down, and the ending was really fantastic, so I'm still excited to keep moving on. But <i>*sigh*</i>, I just wish there had been more of ANYONE except Mal. I will say that I really enjoyed Tolya and Tamar's characters; I think they added an element that invested me into the story further. Here's to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061957.Ruin_and_Rising__The_Shadow_and_Bone_Trilogy___3_" title="Ruin and Rising (The Shadow and Bone Trilogy, #3) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruin and Rising</a>; may it be everything that this one was not and more! <br /><br />********************<br />Buddy read with the fabulous favorite BENTLEY &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="17119548069096970321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
