<div id="review_502526615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/502526615" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/502526615?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-publication">2013-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=june">june</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=macmillan">macmillan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=gorgeous-prose">gorgeous-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mythic-and-fairy-tale-ish">mythic-and-fairy-tale-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer502526615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5879337845104645822"><a href='http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/05/bardugointerview.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Our Conversation with Leigh Bardugo</a> is up, along with an opportunity to win our Siege and Storm ARC!<br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b> <i>Siege and Storm</i> is an exquisite jewel of a book. The second installment in Leigh Bardugo's Grisha Trilogy is full of adventure and magic--and in my view, it's even better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_' title='Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow and Bone</a>.<br/><br/>There are flying ships. A thrilling, poignant scene with a magnificent white ice dragon. A whirling, frenzied volcra attack in the night. A sobering ride through the city of Novokribirsk, where name</span>
  <span id="freeText5879337845104645822" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/05/bardugointerview.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Our Conversation with Leigh Bardugo</a> is up, along with an opportunity to win our Siege and Storm ARC!<br /><br /><b>4.5 stars</b> <i>Siege and Storm</i> is an exquisite jewel of a book. The second installment in Leigh Bardugo's Grisha Trilogy is full of adventure and magic--and in my view, it's even better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a>.<br /><br />There are flying ships. A thrilling, poignant scene with a magnificent white ice dragon. A whirling, frenzied volcra attack in the night. A sobering ride through the city of Novokribirsk, where names are written in blood on church walls and a <i>Ryeal'nye Alina</i>, "genuine Alina" has terrifying meaning. And Genya--oh, my heart breaks for the beautiful Genya. <br /><br />So much thought was put into this world, with evocative settings, original folk tales, gorgeous clothes, memorable battles, and incredibly imaginative touches. (I <i>love</i> the gift from Nikolai's father!) The food porn, both real and imagined, made me dizzy with pleasure: smoked sprats on black bread, little dwarf fruit trees, brandied cuckoo, cold soup served in jeweled pumpkin-shaped cups, croquembouche, and a suckling pig, to name but a few of the items that made my mouth water. And I definitely want to have a baby jello deer at my next party! Preferably with a miniature living forest centerpiece.<br /><br />And while I still hold love for both Mal and The Darkling, there's now also Sturmhond, a dashing privateer with a careless grin and hidden agenda. I can't help it, friends, I have a serious weakness for men who have a gift for witty banter. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He's been added to my fictional island, where swoonworthy YA boys like Will Herondale, Dimitri Belikov, Adrian Ivashkov, and Archer Cross roam about freely like ponies. You may come visit, they're always willing to play.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Alina's interactions with Sturmhond are so much fun to read, and even when he's out of the room, his presence continues to fill it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"So you don't trust me to resist his charms?"<br /><br />"I don't even trust myself. I've never seen anyone work a crowd the way he does. I'm pretty sure the rock and trees are getting ready to swear fealty to him."</i>
</b><br /><br />Most of all, I love how Alina character has undergone interesting development. She begins asserting herself more and more, and the allure of power beckons seductively--but the price she must pay for it may be more than she can afford. <br /><br /><b><i>I looked up at the star-filled sky. The night was velvety black and strewn with jewels. The hunger struck me suddenly. </i>I want them<i>, I thought. All that light, all that power. </i>I want it all.</b><br /><br />Her relationship with Mal is now terribly complicated, both by her position as Sun Summoner and by the position she's put him in. So many YA books revert to tired old machinations to separate love interests, but the tension and difficulty between these two feel urgent and real. <br /><br />I have to say, <i>Shadow and Bone</i> is the only book that all three of us read and loved last year on the blog, and all three of us love this sequel, too! I mean, K says <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/05/siege-and-storm-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">it deserves a meteor shower of stars</a>. What does this mean for book three? Will Leigh Bardugo blow our minds with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061957.Ruin_and_Rising__The_Grisha___3_" title="Ruin and Rising (The Grisha, #3) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruin and Rising</a>? I have the feeling the answer is going to be a resounding YES.<br /><br /><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for this review.</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5879337845104645822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2114857943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer767784991847212919"><b>DNF @ 40%</b><br/><br/>Annnnnnd, I'm gonna wave the white flag here, peeps. <br/><br/>Despite having already read book one...<br/><br/>Despite having ALL three books <i>physically</i> on my shelf...<br/><br/>Despite those books being guarded by my beloved John Wick Funko POP...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1533157057i/26063428._SX540_.jpg' width='496' height='314' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I must bid adieu and part with said technicolor beauties. <br/><br/>Because BORED. <br/>And because life is too short and my shelves too full. <br/><br/>Oh well.<br/>Onward!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533157184ra/26063437.gif' width='344' height='193' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6487640190284557768">Holy freaking crap. <br/><br/>You know when a book is so good... so captivating.. that you cannot find the words to even give it a worthy review? Even now, I find myself without many words to express how much I love this series. <br/><br/><b>So I'm just going to leave you with a few reasons this book is totally legit. </b><br/><br/>1. PIRATES. Snarky ones.<br/>2. STEAMPUNK STEAMPUNK <b>STEAMPUNK!!!!</b><br/>3. BADASS MAGIC<br/>4. YES, this book is much darker than the first.<br/>5. Mind games. Crazy ones. The struggle is real [and swoon worthy]<br/>6. Alina's cha</span>
  <span id="freeText6487640190284557768" style="display:none">Holy freaking crap. <br /><br />You know when a book is so good... so captivating.. that you cannot find the words to even give it a worthy review? Even now, I find myself without many words to express how much I love this series. <br /><br /><b>So I'm just going to leave you with a few reasons this book is totally legit. </b><br /><br />1. PIRATES. Snarky ones.<br />2. STEAMPUNK STEAMPUNK <b>STEAMPUNK!!!!</b><br />3. BADASS MAGIC<br />4. YES, this book is much darker than the first.<br />5. Mind games. Crazy ones. The struggle is real [and swoon worthy]<br />6. Alina's character growth<br />7. Second book syndrome? <b>NOPE.</b> And the last half is bat shit crazy.<br />8. The *thing* that you aren't sure if its real or not.. and the moment you find out if you're right or wrong <i>(anyone?? yeah??)</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Basically when you realize all those times he appeared to her- he was legit there  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />9. GORGEOUS writing. <br />10. THE FREAKING ENDING. LEGIIIITTTTTTTTT. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Yeah.. the moment she's like "My power is yours... and yours is mine..." freaking wow.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />11. The Darkling. Nuff said.<br /><br />I literally could not read fast enough. There is so much emotional struggle - so many challenges, and our dear Alina had to suffer them all... and yet in the end, she was the <b>BALLER</b> that I knew she would be. <br /><br /><b>And I gotta say something about Mal.</b><br /><i> (This isn't super spoilery imo but read at your own risk.)</i><br />He gets a lot of shit in this book for his rash decisions. Most people tend to hate him, but I just can't bring myself to feel anything but sorrow for him. He is just hurting... and <b>
  <i>hurting people hurt people.</i>
</b> And if you ask me, he does get his shot at redemption in the future. Now does that mean I ship him with Alina? I'm not gonna answer that. You'll have to read my review of book 3. <br /><br /><b>Lastly</b>, just a friendly reminder that I compiled a list of songs [that are more or less really just for the Darkling himself...] You can check them out <a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/brilia/playlist/38l294WPXicHHkRWiaemNG" rel="nofollow noopener">here!!!</a><br /><i>**and can I just say that I imagine the song "Frost Flowers" by Evelyn Glennie is perfect for the scene between Alina + the Darkling in his room....</i><br /><br />Ps... I feel like I should note that I read this series on audible. The narrator was absolutely phenomenal. Ohhhh how good she does all the voices... If you have only read the physical copy, I recommend going back through these on audio!<br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

<div id="review_334406021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334406021" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334406021?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=ya-pnr-maddness">ya-pnr-maddness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334406021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13081780433564252411">Sequels are really hard to write reviews for. Mostly because people don’t want to read them for fear of spoilers, but keeping them spoiler free makes it difficult to properly discuss the book. So now I’m going to have to do this review in code.<br/><br/>In Siege and Storm Alina and Mal are on the run from the Darkling. They meet Pumpkin who has the ability to help Alina defeat the Darkling. Problem is, Mal and Pumpkin don’t get on at all. Also, the Darkling can now line dance which adds a level of complic</span>
  <span id="freeText13081780433564252411" style="display:none">Sequels are really hard to write reviews for. Mostly because people don’t want to read them for fear of spoilers, but keeping them spoiler free makes it difficult to properly discuss the book. So now I’m going to have to do this review in code.<br><br>In Siege and Storm Alina and Mal are on the run from the Darkling. They meet Pumpkin who has the ability to help Alina defeat the Darkling. Problem is, Mal and Pumpkin don’t get on at all. Also, the Darkling can now line dance which adds a level of complication. As well as line dancing, which makes a dark and creepy addition to the novel, the Darling drives a wedge between Mal and Alina by knitting. Also, I think he may be losing the plot a little.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380378508i/734178._SY540_.png" alt="Twilight gone mad" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Firstly, Bardugo’s writing has dramatically improved. Siege &amp; Storm is a far smoother novel, both in terms of writing craft and pacing. The tension is always ramped up, the drama meter is set to erupt and before you realize what is happening, it all explodes in your face, leaving you clutching at the tattered remains of your heart and an ego that is no longer ashamed to see you crawl onto twitter to cry on Bardugo’s shoulder.<br><br>I can’t really talk too much about the characters without giving it away – but Alina kicked butt in this installment. Especially when she got hold of her aardvark. No more doe-eyed victim. She really struggles and grapples with her goiter. What does her goiter mean for her? For Mal? For the future of Ravka? And was the Darkling right about that Chinese finger box between Mal and Alina? Mal struggles the most in this novel as he is a salt mine. And in his salt mineyness he deteriorates and loses a lot of faith. I have a feeling he learned a lot about himself in this novel.<br><br>Everyone grows and changes, even the Darkling a little and I wonder if he’ll let Alina continue to cross stitch, or if he’s finally going to seriously back stitch her? Or has his line dancing finally started to shake him up? So many questions, so many moral and ethical dilemmas.<br><br>There is little doubt that Pumpkin stole the show and I applaud Bardugo for his inclusion. He certainly made life interesting and added a great comedic element to the book. Overall, Siege and Storm managed to be a stronger novel than the first. Now I absolutely can’t wait for the next!<br><br>*This review also appears on my blog, <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2013/03/02/review-siege-and-storm-by-leigh-bardugo/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.*<br><br><i>An ARC was provided to me by Macmillan for reviewing purposes. No money or favors were exchanged for this review. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13081780433564252411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2624166549?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2018</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624166549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15047552935175642779">Not sure if I should rate this 1 or 2 stars because this was a pain to get through. I found myself putting off reading it just so that I wouldn't have to engage with this story anymore; when I forced myself to read it I would just speed-read it to get it over with. This very much feels like a filler book because the plot moves slowly, which would be fine if the main characters weren't so bland. What should have been a plot is distracted by trivial relationship issues, and I hated that Alina's lo</span>
  <span id="freeText15047552935175642779" style="display:none">Not sure if I should rate this 1 or 2 stars because this was a pain to get through. I found myself putting off reading it just so that I wouldn't have to engage with this story anymore; when I forced myself to read it I would just speed-read it to get it over with. This very much feels like a filler book because the plot moves slowly, which would be fine if the main characters weren't so bland. What should have been a plot is distracted by trivial relationship issues, and I hated that Alina's love triangle has evolved into a love square. The Darkling was also barely in this book, which I think lessens the intrigue and conflict. Reading "The Tailor" short story at the end was the most engaged &amp; interested I've been in the book compared to the rest of the series. I don't know why Genya is not the main character; following her story with David and Nikolai would have been immensely more interesting, and would add depth to the Darkling as well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15047552935175642779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer633149397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10180642443385296050">I think I might’ve been the only person who had one foot in each of the ‘<u>Shadow and Bone</u> is awesome’ and ‘<u>Shadow and Bone</u> is mediocre’ camps. <u>Siege and Storm</u> was supposed to be the book that made up my mind, but instead, I'm completely split... I truly do see why so many friends have raved about Leigh Bardugo's series - a part of me absolutely feels the same way - yet at the same time, another part, maybe a bigger part, has so many issues with the story I also have half a mind to angrily reject </span>
  <span id="freeText10180642443385296050" style="display:none">I think I might’ve been the only person who had one foot in each of the ‘<u>Shadow and Bone</u> is awesome’ and ‘<u>Shadow and Bone</u> is mediocre’ camps. <u>Siege and Storm</u> was supposed to be the book that made up my mind, but instead, I'm completely split... I truly do see why so many friends have raved about Leigh Bardugo's series - a part of me absolutely feels the same way - yet at the same time, another part, maybe a bigger part, has so many issues with the story I also have half a mind to angrily reject everything about this. I'm pretty sure I'm going to be the odd man out with my half love half loathe view toward this sequel, but I don't think I've ever read a book that's left me so utterly frustrated between my mixed reactions.<br /><br />To put it another way, I once compared <u>Shadow and Bone</u> to a masterfully constructed house of cards, and that's still true of <u>Siege and Storm</u>. It's a beautiful view, and I'd be dishonest if I said I didn't enjoy every minute of looking at it while it stood, and yet, at the same time, when I'm poking around, the whole thing falls apart, and I'd be dishonest too if I said that doesn't bother, nay, enrage me. Here's the thing, Leigh Bardugo is an excellent (some would say superficial) writer in the sense she can pull together character, setting, myth, and plot in a way that's epic, exciting, compelling, and just feels like reading a modern day folk tale, and that got to me, it really did. I'm not going to say I didn't feel what my raving friends felt, because I did - cool world building, tough heroine, epic fantasy, what's not to like?<br /><br />But at the end of the day, Bardugo's talent is really making something out of nothing, because all those great qualities, if you think about it, is just that, nothing. Take for example Alina, who seems like this multifaceted character who has a complex relationship with power, but you know, she can't even answer the most basic question about her character - why is she doing any of this, taking charge, going up against the Darkling? Love of country? Nope, that's not it. Mal? Ha. The Darkling? Are you kidding me? Bardugo does a great job of fabricating this illusion of Alina as a complex and reluctant heroine, but behind the (admittedly awesome) writing, I just didn’t get a sense her character had any drive besides her relationship with Mal or whatever the plot demanded, and it seemed like to me she’s the kind of one dimensional character who can’t exist outside of being swept up by the plot.<br /><br />As for the other characters, the Darkling's this well written, interesting evil character, but behind the facade is... nothing at all. Seriously, we know nothing about the Darkling or his motivations. I’m disappointed because <u>Siege and Storm</u> gave us zero development for his character, and all the praise seems to be directed at a blank slate who’s been the lucky beneficiary of some massive transference. And Mal (a.k.a. uninteresting designated love interest), I honestly don’t know why I tolerate him as much as I do, because his character really doesn’t exist outside of causing Alina angst, this time with well received new guy Sturmhond, who, if you think about it, is just an amalgam of every bad boy stereotype ever in one well written but blatantly cliched package (with one early confrontation scene between him and the Darkling leaving me steaming). Yet I'll admit, Bardugo has skills and she pulls all of this off, creating these seemingly complex characters that shouldn't be, but while part of me has no qualms with liking them, the other part's just irked by how superficial they are.<br /><br />Then again, my view of the plot is just as equally conflicted. On one hand, the pacing, beyond a bizarre turnabout involving the Darkling's reappearance in the first chapter or two, totally worked and had me hooked the whole way through, wondering if Alina could truly beat her nemesis - it's just that riveting. On the other, the plot blatantly screams 'quest to find MacGuffin' and 'obvious rehash of the first book' with pretty much the same structure down to the same convenient nonending, and you know, I <i>liked</i> working my way through the story at the same time that I <i>hated</i> it. Like I said, it's a testament to Leigh Bardugo's skill as a writer that she can make such blatantly shallow elements work in her book, and I love that they work but hate how I can so easily recognize what she's done.<br /><br />Anyway, I have a feeling everyone who loved the first book will love this too. I'm also pretty sure those who didn't will laugh this one off as well. And that leaves me in the middle with my conflicted opinions, anticipating the final book yet griping about my dissatisfaction at the same time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10180642443385296050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And because of that he is dead.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474048204ra/20547767.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>10)<b>I WANT MAL AND ALINA TOGETHER!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497784175ra/23056921.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText3990085271496418326" style="display:none">Can we all just acknowledge the adorableness of David?? He and Nikolai deserve all the stars and to be honest their characters were the saving grace of this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543863911ra/26682496.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alina was very frustrating at times. But I now understand his fears for Alina and his need to prove himself. <br><br>I enjoyed meeting new characters like Tamar and Tolya and Nikolai obviously. But some new characters (*cough* Vasily *cough*) made me so mad. <br><br>Mal and Alina's relationship in this book left me face palming and had me rolling my eyes like crazy. I wanted to shout at both of them. <br><br>As much as I love Nikolai, not for one moment did I ship him with Alina. They just don't fit. <br><br>I get why many fans ship the Darkling and Alina. But I can't get over the things he's done. <br><br>All in all <i>Siege and Storm</i> was a bit slow. There were parts I loved and others that had me gritting my teeth and hoping something is going to happen. <br><br>I really hope things pick up in <i>Ruin and Rising.</i><br>_______<br><b>My reviews for</b> { all books in the Grishaverse} :<br><i>[Grisha Trilogy]</i><br>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2469888928" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2469889580" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruin and Rising</a><br><br><i>[Six of Crows Duology]</i><br>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2598099625" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606611069" rel="nofollow noopener">Crooked Kingdom</a><br><br><i>[Nikolai Series]</i><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2535902543" rel="nofollow noopener">King of Scars</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2535902272" rel="nofollow noopener">Untitled book 2</a><br></span>

<div id="review_1696719383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1696719383" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1696719383?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=memorable-male-characters">memorable-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=almost-great">almost-great</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1696719383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16695652829901444224"><b>3ish Stars <br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/>This is really hard to rate, because I <i>really</i> liked some parts, and really disliked others. <s>Like Mal.</s><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409610745' rel='nofollow noopener'>I really enjoyed the first book,</a> but this series can go in two directions and I’m not sure I like one of them.<br/><br/> In the first novel, Alina constantly called herself a scrawny, 'useless' orphan girl. She had some major self-confidence problems, and her unrequited feelings for the golden-boy (Mal) didn’t help. But then she discovered her powers, met The Darkling and just <i>came int</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16695652829901444224" style="display:none"><b>3ish Stars <br /><br />Overview: </b><br /><br />This is really hard to rate, because I <i>really</i> liked some parts, and really disliked others. <s>Like Mal.</s><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409610745" rel="nofollow noopener">I really enjoyed the first book,</a> but this series can go in two directions and I’m not sure I like one of them.<br /><br /> In the first novel, Alina constantly called herself a scrawny, 'useless' orphan girl. She had some major self-confidence problems, and her unrequited feelings for the golden-boy (Mal) didn’t help. But then she discovered her powers, met The Darkling and just <i>came into her own.</i> <br /><br />She trained with the Grisha and felt powerful, and because she felt it, <i>she was.</i> (Ugh, I loved it.) Then the ending of the first book happened and challenged everything she thought she knew about the Grisha. And this somehow also thrust her back with Mal and back into the role of self-deprecating, scrawny orphan. <br /><br /><u>I feel like the series can either: </u><br />1.	End with her rejecting this complicated, corrupted society and deciding to live as the ‘simple’ girl she was before.<br />2.	Show her embracing the ideas of this culture on her own terms.<br /><br />I’m a fan of #2. But this book couldn’t make up its mind and ended up mostly filler. <br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br />Nikolai is such a fun addition! I love his sense of humor and how it wasn’t compromised by his family/backstory. I just want to grab a beer with him, tbh. <br /><br />Like I know The Darkling is awful and malicious but HE’S SO INTERESTING. He’s such a dynamic character who relies on these manipulative movements. He seems to truly believe he’s doing the best thing (even if I’m not certain what that is yet) and the way he unnerves everyone was <i>fantastic.</i><br /><br />There was more world-building here, which I thought was lacking in the first book. It got a little overtly political in places, but it seemed necessary. This world is so vast and creative and I really enjoy the Russian influences. <br /><br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br /><br />CAN MAL JUST LEAVE<br /><br />There are <i>pages</i> of Alina commenting on how good he is at <i>everything.</i> And I just don’t care? All he does is comment on how he doesn’t want Alina to change and how frustrated he is because things are different and it’s <i>boring.</i> <br /><br />(And side note: Alina was in love with him for <i>years</i> why is she only now interesting to him? What right does he have to be so jealous of everything?)<br /><br />The Darkling and Genya were both so underutilized. Whyyyy? There was so much time with new characters and I just wanted to see them again.<br /><br />So. Much. Filler. Nothing actually happened outside of the first 50 pages and the last 10. It was just Mal and Alina arguing, politics, Alina stressing about herself, politics, Nikolai cracking jokes, politics, everyone wondering what The Darkling’s plan is... Just a ton of build-up. <br /><br />Did we really need another love interest? I like the character. Not digging the romance. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion: </b> <br /><br />I think I’m going to either really hate or love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14061957.Ruin_and_Rising__The_Grisha___3_" title="Ruin and Rising (The Grisha, #3) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruin and Rising</a>, depending on the direction it goes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16695652829901444224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer8440674026368646066"><i> “There are no others like us, Alina. And there never will be.” </i><br/><br/>3.5 ⭐️<br/><br/>Though I am enjoying this series, I’m not finding them to be as amazing as all the hype makes them seem. <br/>Alina has taken her place as the leader of the 2nd army, and preparations are under way to go to war against The Darkling. <br/>Meanwhile, Mal is feeling less and less useful, and constantly jealous of other men who speak to Alina. This girl is supposedly ‘plain looking’ yet at one point she has 4 different men after her?! Like </span>
  <span id="freeText8440674026368646066" style="display:none"><i> “There are no others like us, Alina. And there never will be.” </i><br /><br />3.5 ⭐️<br /><br />Though I am enjoying this series, I’m not finding them to be as amazing as all the hype makes them seem. <br />Alina has taken her place as the leader of the 2nd army, and preparations are under way to go to war against The Darkling. <br />Meanwhile, Mal is feeling less and less useful, and constantly jealous of other men who speak to Alina. This girl is supposedly ‘plain looking’ yet at one point she has 4 different men after her?! Like seriously! Why?! It’s just not necessary IMO. <br />I enjoy reading about the different types of Grisha and Alina’s growth with her powers. <br />Overall I will read the last book just to see what happens, but I’m not particularly bothered with this one. Maybe because I’m getting tired of the whole “plain girl with special powers is the only one able to save the world. Oh and everyone fancies her.” Of course this isn’t the books fault, just that I’ve read a lot like that and this one seems like just another to add to the pile. <br /><br /><i> “You know the problem with heroes and saints...they always end up dead.” </i><br /></span>

<div id="review_2096101706" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101706" />
    <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks"><img alt="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517623708p2/63164992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096101706?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks">Grace (BURTSBOOKS)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63164992-grace-burtsbooks?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096101706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17244433076484383799">3.5 stars. <br/><br/>Hello. Considering this is a sequel I’m just gonna jump into my thoughts… beware spoilers ahead that I’m not tagging because literally anything I write in this review is going to be in some way or another a spoiler. (If you want a synopsis or actual coherent thoughts check out my review of<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101672?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'> Shadow and Bone</a>)<br/><br/>While reading the first book of this trilogy(Shadow and Bone) I was always entertained but I had a big problem getting into the world and the book and just being invested in what was</span>
  <span id="freeText17244433076484383799" style="display:none">3.5 stars. <br /><br />Hello. Considering this is a sequel I’m just gonna jump into my thoughts… beware spoilers ahead that I’m not tagging because literally anything I write in this review is going to be in some way or another a spoiler. (If you want a synopsis or actual coherent thoughts check out my review of<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101672?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Shadow and Bone</a>)<br /><br />While reading the first book of this trilogy(Shadow and Bone) I was always entertained but I had a big problem getting into the world and the book and just being invested in what was happening. That was not a problem with Siege and Storm. It was wayyyyy more interesting. That may be because I read it on audio, which I always enjoy more, or maybe this book is just better. More likely than not though, the reason I liked this book so much was Nikolai Lanstov. <br /><br />Nikolai. Nikolai. Nikolai. Usually, I hate giving in to the hype and being super typical and bandwagoning but honestly he is such a loveably charming and witty character I can’t even be bothered to care. I have never understood the hype about anything more than I have about Nikolai. He deserves every good thing any of us say about him and truthfully saved this series. <br /><br />From the moment Sturmhond was introduced I knew he had to be Nikolai. Not because I knew anything about him going into this book other than the fact that everyone loved him but because he was soooo entertaining and likeable that I couldn’t imagine another character being better than him. And maybe this shows my lack of faith in Leigh Bardugo at this time because I truly just didn’t think she had it in her to introduce two great characters after the bland-fest of Shadow and Bone. <br /><br />Maybe I should have talked about Alina first because I mean she is the main character but come on Nikolai stole the show on this one. She doesn’t read like the main character, or maybe all YA main characters are like this but she just seems like a placeholder, like she’s telling the story but it could have been anyone. The only individual thing about her is her power and if someone else had it I’m not sure the story would be much different. I don’t dislike her, she is a likable character and she really grew into herself and her power throughout this book. She’s sassy and often hilarious and thankfully has developed to not to take anyone’s shit but still I feel like there’s something missing. I really don’t know. I just wish she were less ordinary.<br /><br />Now that I sorted through those thoughts, let’s talk about Mal. <br /><br />One of my biggest complaints in Shadow and Bone was that I had literally no understanding of who the hell Mal was. He was supposedly Alina’s best friend but I just couldn’t place who he was as a character and how his actions coincided with that. That wasn’t a problem in this book and I guess for that reason I can’t exactly complain but Jesus Christ was he stupid. I get that he’s insecure and all that. He’s very prideful and has a frail grasp on his masculinity but can he shut the hell up for one moment? <br /><br />He supposedly loves Alina but the version of her that he wants doesn’t even exist anymore. The Alina of their childhood was frail, quiet, unassuming and did little more than fuel his ego. Once he realizes she’s changed he tells her about his feelings and then continues to complain for the majority of the second book about this very fact. He can’t handle her power because it makes her more confident than he is. <br /><br />The worst part is The Darkling warns Alina about this very problem and nothing angers me more than The Darling being right….. still waiting to understand why people like that guy. I mean he’s a power-hungry manipulator. I just don’t get it. <br /><br />All of these complaints are not to say that I don’t like this book because I do, I really do. If I didn’t I wouldn’t talk about any of these things because I wouldn’t even care. As negative as I sound I care about this book. I care about these characters even when they make me want to rip my hair out. None of the things I’m complaining about would really make me want to lower my rating of it. <br /><br />Something that I actually had a real problem with was the fact that there were only four major characters in this novel and apart from Alina all of them were men, which is a problem in and of its self but also all of them were for some reason romantically interested in her. Why can’t male and female’s coincide together and thrive in mutually beneficial relationships that don’t involve romance? Is that too much to ask for? (I'M LOOKING @ YOU NIKOLAI)<br /><br />This isn’t even to mention that Alina is boring as fuck. Idk why someone like Nikolai or even the ancient fucking powerful ass Darkling would have feelings for her. Like yes on a base level I get that they like her power or whatever but still… it’s just unrealistic.<br /><br />Ummm, I think that’s all I have to say. This was a mess of thoughts cause I never know how tf to talk about sequels. This was more my thoughts on the actual events of the book rather than the writing which is what I usually talk about but yeah other than Nikolai this book followed the same format more or less as the first. Solid writing, entertaining events, same bland ass characters only this time they whine more. Somehow I still liked it, and somehow I care about Mal and Alina. <br /><br />The end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17244433076484383799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_846264383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/846264383" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/846264383?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer846264383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16851690720148822499"><b>Read 2 | March 2019</b><br/><br/>Now oddly enough I didn't love this as much the second time! It's still a solid 4-stars, but I remember thinking this was the best of the trilogy? huh. my main thing is: wow it was slow. The travelling scenes, the political chats around a war table...I'm just like, my son, I thought there was a lot more action and banter here. But the finale is frikkin fantastic. And I will take every second I can with Nikolai, who is a gift to this world and absolutely knows it. Bless his dec</span>
  <span id="freeText16851690720148822499" style="display:none"><b>Read 2 | March 2019</b><br /><br />Now oddly enough I didn't love this as much the second time! It's still a solid 4-stars, but I remember thinking this was the best of the trilogy? huh. my main thing is: wow it was slow. The travelling scenes, the political chats around a war table...I'm just like, my son, I thought there was a lot more action and banter here. But the finale is frikkin fantastic. And I will take every second I can with Nikolai, who is a gift to this world and absolutely knows it. Bless his deceitful slytherin happy soul.<br /><br />(Also utterly glowering at Mal for that scene where he thinks Alina rejects him and then he goes off in a storming tantrum? can we talk about toxic masculinity, mate.)<br /><br /><br />*:·ﾟ✧*:·ﾟ✧<br /><b>Read 1 | April 2015</b><br /><br /><br /><b>That was <i>incredible</i>.</b> WHICH PLEASES ME GREATLY. I've had a whole run of 3-star reads and then I couldn't really remember the plot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18217960.Shadow_and_Bone___Siege_and_Storm__Grisha_Verse__1_2_" title="Shadow and Bone &amp; Siege and Storm (Grisha Verse #1-2) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone &amp; Siege and Storm</a> (AGH!!) but thank goodness for the <a href="http://recaptains.co.uk/2013/03/shadow-and-bone-by-leigh-bardugo/" rel="nofollow noopener">Recaptains blog recap on book 1</a>. It saved my life, quite frankly. And made me love book 2 so so much.<br /><br />OKAY. LEMME WRITE A LIST. And this'll probably have spoilers for book 1, but only little teeny tiny ones. Like the fact that Mal and Alina are sort of a <i>thing</i> and the Darkling is abroad in the universe being darkling-ish. As he does. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>THINGS I LIKED A LOT:</blockquote>
</b><br /><br /><b> + I loved Alina's journey into dark and villainy.</b> Gosh, that sounds awful of me BUT I SPEAK TRUTH! She's really really changed and I love her character development. Talk about EPIC. She's gotten so much darker, and she <i>likes</i> the power. And at the same time she's torn between wanting to save the world and being good and yada ya. Basically she rocks. And she's a little scary.<br /><b> + Sturmhond. THAT IS ALL.</b> oh. my. gosh, peoples, he is ADORABLE. He's like Jack Sparrow meets Thorne from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13206760.Scarlet__The_Lunar_Chronicles___2_" title="Scarlet (The Lunar Chronicles, #2) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a>. He's sassy and funny and quick. AND he's smart. He's like a super-smart dude who invents stuff (like flying boats) and wants the best for his kingdom and afdjslk, I love Sturmhond. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I also love that he's the prince and that he's, for once, not running away from a crown. Usually princes are like "GIVE M FREEDOM." But Nikolai is totally embracing it and wanting o be king. Refreshing? YES. Exciting? YES. Adorable? OMG YES.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>+ As always, Russia-ish fantasy rocks.</b> I've had enough of Eastern Europe fantasy to last a life time so THANK THE SNOWY PINNACLES for this delicious Russian blast. Although, I noticed, it's almost steampunky here. They actually have pistols and inventions. So super super refreshing.<br /><b> + I really love the writing style!</b> It keeps my eyeballs glued to the page! I wasn't even skimming in this book! (I'm a notorious skimmer.) And the humour was A+. I was giggling all over the place.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>STUFF I DIDN'T LIKE, AND BASICALLY MADE ME SCREAM:</blockquote>
</b><br /><br /><b> + Mal.</b> Oh, Mal. Oh, go jump off a cliff, perhaps? I feel mildly bad (pfft, I do not) for not liking OR shipping him with ALina but Mal has issues. He's the "main love interest" but he's so self-involved and dramatic. Things go wrong, he goes off and sulks. Alina's struggling with massive power and darkness and freaking out of her MIND?! What does Mal do? Has a tantrum because she flinched when he touched her. YEAH MAL, MAYBE THE GIRL IS SUFFERING FROM PTSD, EH? He's so so self-involved! He's not there for her. She's trying to save the world and do the right thing politically <i>and</i> now she has to be there so his feelings don't get hurt? PUH-LEASE. I don't like Mal.<br /><b> + Not as much action as I was hoping for.</b> Although, don't get me wrong, this is NOT a filler sequel-blues book. It's incredible and I loved it. The beginning is really exciting, but the last 40% was sort of political and talkative and invention-y and just...eh. I was too angry at Mal the whole time and didn't really enjoy it.<br /><b>+ CLIFFHANGER. ARGHH!!!</b> I'm joking. This isn't bad. It did make me scream, but I LOVE cliffhangers. I want book 3, asap. (And my library doesn't have it, so yeah, that's me crying in the corner over there.)<br /><br /><br /><b>THIS BOOK IS GREAT.</b> I was a bit dubious and worried I wouldn't love it, considering I wasn't <i>in love</i> with book 1 (I totally enjoyed book 1, I just wasn't as taken as most readers seem to be). I love Russia-ness. I love Alina. I love that I hate Darkling. I love Sturmhond. <br /><br />Mostly, though, to be honest, I love Sturmhond.<br /><br /><b>NOTABLE QUOTES OF AWESOME:</b><br /><br /><blockquote>“I took a breath. “Your highness—”<br />“Nikolai,” he corrected. “But I’ve also been known to answer to ‘sweetheart’ or ‘handsome.” </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Mal crossed his arms and considered the privateer. "I can't decide if you're crazy or stupid."<br />"I have so many good qualities," Sturmhond said. "It can be hard to choose.” </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>“You heard Prince Perfect," Mal said, and joined us at the table. <br />Nikolai grinned. "I've had a lot of nicknames, but that one is easily the most accurate.” </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>“You just punched a prince, Alina. I guess we can add one more act of treason to our list.”<br />I shook out my sore hand. My knuckles smarted. “First of all, are we so sure he really is a prince? And second, you’re just jealous.”<br />“Of course I’m jealous. I thought I was going to get to punch him. That isn’t the point.” </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="16851690720148822499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WkBptnKiV4UxuPG3TLjVn9/4tG4oqZF0rLAmKOy7CMrGvd3TlfY4IclzV01d/M4EzJZFMoDYnz+IN4lKLEs8KQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rzNY9NgYBugebTv/79gdiiCfKtU30p3KXHKi2b8P+lIzzuyRP0xpTOamnQX+nAYRM/HbiZ+jk4F49Q27f//OsQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10640894163997659736">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction & Fantasy. Her other works include Wo</span>
  <span id="freeText10640894163997659736" style="display:none">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy. Her other works include Wonder Woman: Warbringer and Ninth House (Goodreads Choice Winner for Best Fantasy 2019) which is being developed for television by Amazon Studios. Leigh was born in Jerusalem, grew up in Southern California, and graduated from Yale University. These days she lives and writes in Los Angeles. For information on new releases and appearances, sign up for her <a href="https://https//leighbardugo.us11.list-manage.com/subscribe?u=160b0462d4826c60dbb8af320&amp;id=ec014907b2" rel="nofollow noopener">newsletter</a>.<br /><br />She would be delighted if you followed her on <a href="http://twitter.com/Lbardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, elated if you visited her at <a href="http://leighbardugo.com" rel="nofollow noopener">LeighBardugo.com</a>, and fairly giddy if you liked her selfies on <a href="http://instagram.com/lbardugo/7" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>. <br /><br /></span>
